  <script type="text/javascript">
   // method to grab query string parameters
var qs = (function(a) {
    if (a == "") return {};
    var b = {};
    for (var i = 0; i &lt; a.length; ++i)
    {
        var p=a[i].split('=', 2);
        if (p.length == 1)
            b[p[0]] = "";
        else
            b[p[0]] = decodeURIComponent(p[1].replace(/\+/g, " "));
    }
    return b;
})(window.location.search.substr(1).split('&amp;'));

// log query string
console.log(qs);

// if UTM Source is not set
qs['utm_source']	= IAS_Set('utm_source');
qs['utm_content']	= IAS_Set('utm_content');

// write IAS pixel
//document.write('&lt;scr' + 'ipt type="text/javascript" src="http://pixel.adsafeprotected.com/jload?anId=7399&amp;advId=STACK&amp;campId=&amp;pubId=' + qs['utm_source'] + '&amp;chanId=' + qs['utm_content'] + '&amp;placementId=header"&gt;&lt;/scr' + 'ipt&gt;&lt;noscript&gt;&lt;img src="http://pixel.adsafeprotected.com/?anId=7399&amp;advId=STACK&amp;campId=&amp;pubId=' + qs['utm_source'] + '&amp;chanId=' + qs['utm_content'] + '&amp;placementId=header" height="1" width="1" alt=""&gt;&lt;/noscript&gt;');

// output IAS pixel into console
//console.log('&lt;scr' + 'ipt type="text/javascript" src="http://pixel.adsafeprotected.com/jload?anId=7399&amp;advId=STACK&amp;campId=&amp;pubId=' + qs['utm_source'] + '&amp;chanId=' + qs['utm_content'] + '&amp;placementId=header"&gt;&lt;/scr' + 'ipt&gt;&lt;noscript&gt;&lt;img src="http://pixel.adsafeprotected.com/?anId=7399&amp;advId=STACK&amp;campId=&amp;pubId=' + qs['utm_source'] + '&amp;chanId=' + qs['utm_content'] + '&amp;placementId=header" height="1" width="1" alt=""&gt;&lt;/noscript&gt;');

// method to set the variables needed for IAS from query string, cookie or default 
function IAS_Set(param)
{
	if (typeof qs[param] == 'undefined')
	{
		var cookie 	= getCookie(param);

		// check to see if we have a cookie
		if (cookie != "")
		{
			// return the cookie value
			return cookie;

		} else {

			// no query string nor cookie values are set, lets return default value
			return "no_" + param;
		}

	} else {

		// set cookie with value (for later use)
		setCookie(param,qs[param],30);

		// query string parameter is set, return its value
		return qs[param];
	}
}

// code "borrowed" from http://www.w3schools.com/js/js_cookies.asp
function getCookie(cname) {
    var name = cname + "=";
    var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
    for(var i=0; i&lt;ca.length; i++) {
        var c = ca[i];
        while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1);
        if (c.indexOf(name) != -1) return c.substring(name.length,c.length);
    }
    return "";
}

// code "borrowed" from http://www.w3schools.com/js/js_cookies.asp
function setCookie(cname, cvalue, exdays) {
    var d = new Date();
    d.setTime(d.getTime() + (exdays*24*60*60*1000));
    var expires = "expires="+d.toUTCString();
    document.cookie = cname + "=" + cvalue + "; " + expires;
}

	            show    = $('.channel_recent li:visible').size()+6;

	            // make sure we're not going above how many total items there are (in this case 60)
	            if (show &lt; 60)

	            }
	            else
	            {

  <script type="text/javascript">
   var isMobile = {
    Android: function() {
        return navigator.userAgent.match(/Android/i);
    },
    BlackBerry: function() {
        return navigator.userAgent.match(/BlackBerry/i);
    },
    iOS: function() {
        return navigator.userAgent.match(/iPhone|iPad|iPod/i);
    },
    Opera: function() {
        return navigator.userAgent.match(/Opera Mini/i);
    },
    Windows: function() {
        return navigator.userAgent.match(/IEMobile/i);
    },
    any: function() {
        return (isMobile.Android() || isMobile.BlackBerry() || isMobile.iOS() || isMobile.Opera() || isMobile.Windows());
    }
};

$is_mobile 	= isMobile.any();

                                                                                    //if (typeof console == "undefined") {window.console = {log: function (m) {alert(m)}};} // Turn console.log into alert if unavailble
 
	var players = [];	// array to hold players
 	var player;
 	var videoPlayer;

	function onTemplateLoad (id) {
		// Add each player's id to the players array
		console.log(id + " loaded");
		players.push(id);
	}
 
	function onTemplateReady (event) {
		// Add a PLAY event handler to each player
		player = brightcove.api.getExperience(event.target.experience.id);
		videoPlayer = player.getModule(brightcove.api.modules.APIModules.VIDEO_PLAYER);
		videoPlayer.addEventListener(brightcove.api.events.MediaEvent.PLAY, function(event) {onPlay(event);});
		videoPlayer.addEventListener(brightcove.api.events.MediaEvent.STOP, function(event) {onStop(event);});
	}

                                                                                   <script type="text/javascript">
                                                                                    var defaultTimeout 		= 5000;
var timeoutReference	= setTimeout(function(){
	DblVerResponse(null);
},defaultTimeout);

function DblVerResponse(response)
{
	// timeout no longer needed
	clearTimeout(timeoutReference);

	// see if we've timed out
	if (response === null)
		handleT();

	else if (response.responseTypeId == 1 &amp;&amp; response.ifb)
		handleB();

	else if (response.responseTypeId == 1 &amp;&amp; ! response.ifb)
		handleH();

	else
		handleE();
}


function handleT() 
{
	// show banner
	show_banners();
    _DVTrack('timeout');
}

function handleB() 
{
	// do not show banner
    _DVTrack('bot');
}

function handleH()
{
	// show banner
	show_banners();
    _DVTrack('human');
}

function handleE()
{
	// show banner
	show_banners();
    _DVTrack('error');
}
function show_banners()
{
	return false;
}

function _DVTrack(type)
{
    // initialize variables
    var protocol        = "";
    var domain          = "www.stack.com";
    var uri             = "/2014/03/12/fast-twitch-muscles/";
    var query_string    = "articlename=fast-twitch-muscles";
    var source          = "";
    var campaign        = "";
    var medium          = "";
    var content         = "";

    // intiialize JSON POST
    var post    = {
        type:           type,
        protocol:       protocol,
        domain:         domain,
        uri:            uri,
        query_string:   query_string,
        source:         source,
        campaign:       campaign,
        medium:         medium,
        content:        content    
    };

    // stringify post variables
    var json    = JSON.stringify(post);

    // make the ajax call
    $.ajax({
        url:        "/API/DoubleVerify/Track.php",
        type:       'POST',
        data:       JSON.parse(json),
        success:    function(data){

            obj   = JSON.parse(data);
            console.log('[EVENT] Track Double Verify Response');
            console.log(obj);
        },
        error:    function(xhr,resp,error){

            // write error to console
            console.log(error);
        }
    }); 
}

document.body.appendChild(script);

                                                                                        var player;
							var modVP;
							var experienceModule;
							var nextVideo = 0;
							var articlePageVideos = new Array(2766818768001,3891661756001,3779966486001);
							var articlePageVideoTitles = new Array('Elite Performance With Mike Boyle: Build Core Strength With Anti-Extension Exercises','Elite Performance with Mike Boyle: Intro to the Functional Movement Screen','World-Class Workouts With Todd Durkin: Build Explosive Speed With Lower-Body Power Drills');
							
							function myTemplateLoaded(experienceID) {
								player = brightcove.api.getExperience(experienceID);
								var APIModules = brightcove.api.modules.APIModules;
								adModule = player.getModule(APIModules.ADVERTISING);
								modVP = player.getModule(APIModules.VIDEO_PLAYER);
								experienceModule = player.getModule(APIModules.EXPERIENCE);
								adModule.addEventListener(brightcove.api.events.AdEvent.START,onAdStart);
								NeonPlayerTracker.onTemplateLoad(experienceID);
							
								adModule.getAdPolicy(setUpAdPolicy);
							}
									function setUpAdPolicy(adPolicy) {
									var newAdPolicy = adPolicy;

									// display preroll
									newAdPolicy.prerollAds = true;
									newAdPolicy.prerollAdKeys = "key=strengthtrainingsection,key1=powertrainingsection,key2=exercisessection";
									adModule.setAdPolicy(newAdPolicy);
								}
								
							function onTemplateReady(evt) {
								//modVP.loadVideoByID(articlePageVideos[nextVideo]);
								modVP.addEventListener(brightcove.api.events.MediaEvent.BEGIN, onMediaBegin);
								modVP.addEventListener(brightcove.api.events.MediaEvent.COMPLETE, onMediaComplete);
								NeonPlayerTracker.onTemplateReady(evt);

								_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'player_3336114731001', 'ready'])
							}
							
							window.onresize = function(newWidth) {
								var BCLcontainingBlock = document.getElementById("BCLcontainingBlock");
								experienceModule.setSize(BCLcontainingBlock.offsetWidth,BCLcontainingBlock.offsetHeight);
							}

							function onMediaBegin(evt) {

								console.log("*****************************");
								console.log(evt);
								console.log("*****************************");

								views(evt.media.id);

								_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'player_3336114731001', 'video_start'])

								document.getElementById("mediaLegend").innerHTML = "Now Playing";
								document.getElementById("mediaDescription").innerHTML = evt.media.shortDescription;
								document.getElementById("mediaInfo").innerHTML = "&lt;a href='#'&gt;" + evt.media.displayName + "&lt;/a&gt;";
								nextVideoTitleIndex = nextVideo+1;
								if (nextVideoTitleIndex == articlePageVideoTitles.length) {
									nextVideoTitleIndex = 0;
								}
								document.getElementById("NextVideo").innerHTML = "Next Video: " + articlePageVideoTitles[nextVideoTitleIndex];
							
							}

							function onAdStart(evt) {

								_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'player_3336114731001', 'preroll_start'])

								document.getElementById("mediaLegend").innerHTML = "Coming Up";
								document.getElementById("mediaInfo").innerHTML = "&lt;a href='http://www.stack.com/video/" + articlePageVideos[nextVideo] + "/" +  encodeURIComponent(articlePageVideoTitles[nextVideo]) + " '&gt;" + articlePageVideoTitles[nextVideo] + "&lt;/a&gt;";

								nextVideoTitleIndex = nextVideo+1;
								if (nextVideoTitleIndex == articlePageVideoTitles.length) {
									nextVideoTitleIndex = 0;
								}
								document.getElementById("NextVideo").innerHTML = "Next Video: " + articlePageVideoTitles[nextVideoTitleIndex];
							}
							function onMediaComplete(evt) {

								_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'player_3336114731001', 'video_complete'])

								document.getElementById("mediaDescription").innerHTML = "";
								loadNextVideo();
							}
							function loadNextVideo() {
								nextVideo++;
								if (nextVideo == articlePageVideos.length) {
									nextVideo = 0;
								}
								views(articlePageVideos[nextVideo]);
								modVP.loadVideoByID(articlePageVideos[nextVideo]);
								document.getElementById("mediaInfo").innerHTML = "&lt;a href='http://www.stack.com/video/" + articlePageVideos[nextVideo] + "/" +  encodeURIComponent(articlePageVideoTitles[nextVideo]) + " '&gt;" + articlePageVideoTitles[nextVideo] + "&lt;/a&gt;";
								return false;
							}
							function loadPrevVideo() {
								nextVideo--;
								if (nextVideo &lt; 0 ) {
									nextVideo = articlePageVideos.length-1;
								}
								views(articlePageVideos[nextVideo]);
								modVP.loadVideoByID(articlePageVideos[nextVideo]);
								return false;
							}

							function views(id) {

								// create POST array 
								var poster 	= {
									"id": 		id,
									"fields":	"playsTotal"
								};

								// JSON encode 
								var json 	= JSON.stringify(poster);

								// update video views 
								_video_views("/API/Brightcove/Video/Get.php",json,"videoViews");
							}

							function _video_views(url,json,elem)
							{
								// make the ajax call
								$.ajax({
									url: 		url,
									type: 		'POST',
									data: 		JSON.parse(json),
									success: 	function(data){

										var response 	= "";
										obj 	= JSON.parse(data);

										console.log(obj);

										if (obj.data.playsTotal.replace(/\,/g,"") &gt; 1000) {
											// show response
											response 	= "Views: " + obj.data.playsTotal;
										} else {
											response 	= "";
										}

										$("#" + elem).html(response);
									},
									error: 		function(xhr,resp,error){

										// write error to console
										console.log(error);
									}
								});	
							}

							// initialize views 
							views(2766818768001);
                                                                                       </script>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        So you want to be as strong as the Hulk, as fast as Flash and as awesome as Superman. The secret to unlocking that superhuman potential may lie within your muscles. Your muscle fibers have a lot of influence what you excel at, whether it's crushing long-distance marathons or finishing 100-meter sprints in the blink of an eye.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Muscle fibers are classified into two main groups Type I (slow twitch) and Type II (fast twitch). Type II fibers are further broken down into subclasses IIa, fast twitch oxidative-glycolytic) and IIx, fast-twitch non-oxidative.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        Type I (Slow Twitch, Oxidative)
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <ul>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Slow contracting
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Slow fatiguing
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Small diameter
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         High number of mitochondria
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         High oxidative capacity (using fat stores as energy)
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Good for low intensity prolonged activities such as maintaining posture and running long distances
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                       </ul>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        Type IIa (Fast Twitch, Oxidative-Glycolytic)
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <ul>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Good number of mitochondria
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Can use both fat stores and glycogen stores for energy
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Resistant to fatigue and recover quickly
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Good for fast, repetitive, low-intensity activity. Bodybuilders posses high numbers of Type IIa muscle fibers, and research suggests they play a big role in muscle size.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                       </ul>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        Type IIx (Fast Twitch, Non-Oxidative)
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <ul>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Low number of mitochondria
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Large in diameter
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Fast fatiguing
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Good for high-intensity, large-power output, such as field events and power lifting.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                       </ul>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        Role of Fast-Twitch Fibers in Sports
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Type II fibers are involved in any activity that includes a quick explosive movement or the rapid development of power. If you play any field sport (shot put, high jump, etc.), football, hockey or sports that don't involve long, slow repetitive movements, it would be in your best interest to develop your fast-twitch muscle fibers.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        The quicker you can recruit your Type II fibers, the more power you can develop. This will give you faster sprint times and help you lift heavier weights and jump higher.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        The biggest reason Type II fibers develop more power then Type I is because the Type IIx fiber can contract 10 times faster than the Type I fiber.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        Can People Be Born With More Type II Muscle Fibers?
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        No two people are built the same. Just as people are born with different bone structures and different levels of hormones, the same is true for muscle fibers. You may be better suited for running long distances (Type I) or explosive bursts of power (Type IIx), or you may be in the middle (Type IIa).
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Some people are born with more fast-twitch muscle fibers than others. But cheer upwith training, you can change your ratio of fast-twitch to slow-twitch muscle fibers.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        Training for Fast-Twitch Muscle Fibers
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        There are a number of ways to increase your ratio of Type II fibersheavy strength training, speed training, plyometric training and Olympic lift training. Training does a few things:
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <ol>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Hypertrophy of the Type II fibers, increasing their power output.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Help recruit Type II fibers faster.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Change Type I fibers to Type II fibers.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                       </ol>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Strength training and speed training can be very effective in developing maximum force. Lifting a heavy weight with slow acceleration will develop maximum force, but you can also achieve maximum force by lifting a lighter weight with fast acceleration. Heavy Squats, Deadlifts and Bench Presses are good ways to increase Type II fibers. So is running sprints, agility drills and med ball training.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Plyometric training and Olympic lifting are also effective fast-twitch fiber recruiters. They do it by using the stretch shortening cycle (SSC), which involves a pre-stretch of the muscle followed by a rapid contraction of the same muscle, resulting in the production of maximum force. Effective exercises include Vertical Jumps, Broad Jumps, Power Cleans, Power Snatches and Depth Jumps.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Long-distance endurance training (running and cycling) and lifting lighter weights for high reps will develop slow-twitch muscle fibers. Unless you want to decrease your fast-twitch muscle fibers, you should limit the amount of endurance training, allotting time for it separate from your strength and power training.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <h2>
                                                                                        Fast-Twitch Muscle Workout Routine
                                                                                       </h2>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        Hang Clean
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Uses the whole body to develop power.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <div class="inline_ad" id="inlineAd">
                                                                                        <div id="x61">
                                                                                        </div>
                                                                                       </div>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        <strong>
                                                                                         Coaching Points
                                                                                        </strong>
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <ul>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Start with your feet under your hips.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Keep your weight close to your body. Don't let it drift away.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Start with light weights and grove the pattern.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                       </ul>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        <strong>
                                                                                         Sets/Reps
                                                                                        </strong>
                                                                                        : 4-6x1-5, rest90 seconds to 3 minutes
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        Med Ball Cross Behind Side Toss
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Med Ball exercises are another great way to develop max power. They are also easier to learn than Olympic lifts. The Med Ball Cross Behind Side Toss is an excellent exercise for developing rotational power for sports like baseball, golf and shot put. You start with one of your shoulders facing a wall. The med ball starts at your back hip. You then cross your back leg behind your front leg, step forward with your front leg and step through with your back leg. When you finish, your hips face the wall.
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        <strong>
                                                                                         Coaching Points
                                                                                        </strong>
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <ul>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Force is created from the hips. Think about rotating your hips as fast as you can, not so much about throwing the ball.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Keep your core tight.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Load your back leg to start and finish with weight on your front leg.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                       </ul>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        <strong>
                                                                                         Sets/Reps:
                                                                                        </strong>
                                                                                        3-6x3-6, rest90 seconds to 3 minutes
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <h3>
                                                                                        PAP Complex
                                                                                       </h3>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Perform a heavy lift at 85% to 95% of your 1 RM, followed by an explosive movement. Another way to look at it, as Russian researcher Yuri Verkhoshansky puts it, is to visualize lifting a can half full of water, but thinking it is full. The end result: lifting the can of water twice as fast. There are a lot of ways to set up the PAP Complex:
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <ul>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Heavy Bench Press followed by a Med Ball Chest Pass or Shot Put throw
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Heavy Squats followed by a Vertical Jump
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Heavy Deadlift followed by a Broad Jump
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Heavy Sled Drag followed by Sprints
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                       </ul>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        <strong>
                                                                                         Key Considerations
                                                                                        </strong>
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <ul>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         Not for beginner athletes.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         May be best used for a one-time max test (Vertical Jump or Sprint)
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                        <li>
                                                                                         May work better for people with a higher ratio of Type II muscle fibers.
                                                                                        </li>
                                                                                       </ul>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        <strong>
                                                                                         Sets/Reps:
                                                                                        </strong>
                                                                                        4-6x3-5 (each exercise), rest90 seconds to 3 minutes (between strength and power exercise)
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        <strong>
                                                                                         Reference:
                                                                                        </strong>
                                                                                       </p>
                                                                                       <p>
                                                                                        Verkhoshansky, Y. V. , and M. C. Siff.
                                                                                        <em>
                                                                                         Supertraining
                                                                                        </em>
                                                                                        . Supertraining Institute, 2009. print.
                                                                                       </p>

                                                                                      function _modal_load_more(mclass)
		{
			// intiailize variables
			var counter = 1;

			// iterate ajax classes
			$("." + mclass).each(function(){
				if ($(this).hasClass('hidden') &amp;&amp; counter &lt;= 2)
				{
					$(this).removeClass('hidden');
					counter = counter + 1;
				}
			});

			return;
		}

function getFileNameTop(siteName)
{
	var strFileName;
	var intLocation;
	var strSiteName;

	//strSiteName = "www.stack.com";
	strSiteName = siteName;
	strFileName = document.location.pathname;

	//pathname starts at host URL and a slash so it will always return one slash
	if (strFileName.length == 1)
	{
		//this has to be set for the default file for the site!
		strFileName = "/index.php";
	}

	return strSiteName + strFileName;
}

	$("body").scrollTop(0);
});

	$("body").scrollTop(document.documentElement.scrollTop+1);
